RATING: 2
The theming, components, etc. are nice, but I think as a "game" (in the sense of a decision-making, intellectually challenging game) it is entirely unplayable as-is.  The large part of the game, until the heli-pad appears, is largely pointless.  In order for the game to work as it should, namely as a "light" game with a good theme and nice components, the victory condition should be completely rewritten, and the game tweaked to be a 20 to 30-minute game.  IMO, a 60-minute+ game in which most of what you do throughout the course of the game do not matter is WRONG.  If it's a 15-minute game, that's okay.

RATING: 5
Have only played one of  the modes that is not a scenario. Probably better playing a scenario. I felt that most of the equipment cards was tied to a location, so you had to go there to use them. Which was pointless when the helipad was discovered. The rules is not as tight and the randomness is maybe a tad high for my taste. Also felt that in the beginning, there was no point moving zombies, as you couldn't block a person completely or overwhelm him. In the end there was no more bullets to get on the map, so it was just a grind to get to the helipad.

Also the map pieces could have been printed on a card board. On a smooth surface, they moved too much.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
This game often gets a bit of an unfair treatment when compared with other zombie themed games but if you tweak a few issues it has it works much better.

For example, there is a great co-op variant for two or more players to team up - but you can still only get two people on the chopper. If you're team mate falls at the last minute do you run back to help him (must be done before it reaches the fallen players turn again) or do you leave him to die and make for the chopper yourself? 

You can also roll one die to determine who will move the zombies (6 numbers for 6 players, 3 pairs for 3 players, and discard 1 or 2 numbers in 4-5 player games) and then that person rolls again to determine how many zombies can be moved.

It's not a great game by far but the option to backstab people is appealing - sometimes.

RATING: 5
The subject is great!  Zoooombieeees!  Heh.  I spend most of the game making zombie grunts and saying "Brains.  More brains" everytime someone moves or places a zombie.

All kidding aside, the game itself suffers from one problem.  It's slow to set up the board.  While one player is messing around with zombies and counters the other players tend to get restless.

Our group is working on some sort of house rule to speed up the board setup phase of the game.

RATING: 8
A great game that can sometime be frustrating because of the tile drawing mechanic used to build the city. I highly recommend you use the quick play option and place the helicopter tile in the bottom third or half of the deck otherwise you can find yourself contending with a sea of zombies.  I very much like that death is never absolute, you start with a fresh character, so everyone can stay in the game and remain effective.

Card cycling is important - use the discard option as often as you can.

RATING: 6
Zombies!!! is a decent game for the right group of players. It is very basic, so it's easy for anyone to pick up and go. However, it tends to take a very long time to finish a game, especially if you're playing with any of the expansions.

There are too many random elements to allow for much strategy, and it is almost always better to attempt to win by killing at least 25 zombies than to actually reach the helipad.

It's a decent game if I'm in the right mood, but I wouldn't necessarily recommend it for hardcore gamers.

RATING: 8
So simple I played it with my 5 y.o. son... to his mother's horrified dismay :). It's a light game.

This is a nice miniature game specially if you like the zombie theme. The art is great and so are the components. There are plenty of fan-made rule variants on the official site; we play with the one where the number of hearts (health) determines the movement range.

Contrary to some comments, I believe the rules and the cards' effects are reasonably clear. It's not because there's an official FAQ and many variants that a game's broken.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
Ugh... Where do I start?

-I don't really like the theme, but even if I loved it, I probably wouldn't enjoy the game. I find theme to be extremely poorly implemented. Most bleeding example: Ok, you've died. There, go back to the beginning (which can be even an improvement to your overall position, effectively being a prize for doing badly). It's not only that the mechanic is anticlimactic, it's that it even works against the theme!

-More on that. I've been carrying this baseball bat all around town. I can only use it on the sports shop (Not sure if the example is actually in the game or not, but it's representative enough). Yeah, sure, that makes sense :what:
I realize it is supposed to be a "You actually only get the bat when you get to the sports shop", but it makes no sense you can get the card at any time and only be able to use it somewhere specifically. Wouldn't it make more sense to have a "you find something cool" card that lets you select an specific item related to the position you're in, and let you use the item whenever you want?

-The 25-zombie kills makes no sense thematically, either: "OK, I've killed 25 zombies. I'm invincible! [Well, I died twice to get to that 25-zombie mark, but that's not all that important, is it?] Fuck the fact that I'm in the middle of the city with no way out and those 5000 other zombies lurking every single street. I've won!"
I understand that rule it's there as a mean to prevent never ending games, but taking into account it also fails on that account, could have it been that bad to add "Kill 25 zombies and exit town by arriving at a tile where the road ends in the table" or something like that? At least it would make more sense...

-Final rant on theme... Zombie games are the kind of theme that screams "cooperative" to me. I can buy you're fighting to survive, though, even if it means standing over your fellow survivor's corpse (Ups, you can'd actually do that, they re-spawn :shake:), but what sense does it makes that another player, minding his business on the other end of the town can actively trump your progress?

-Strategy doesn't mean anything. This game is such a luckfest. You might as well play the Game of Goose, or Chutes and Ladders, your options are almost as limited.

-It's Slooooooooww... and annoyingly long.

Yeah, I hate this game. If I don't play it ever again, it will be too soon. And yeah, I know I bash on the theme a lot, maybe even too much. I can play not-so-thematic games just fine. I love abstracts. But I really dislike when a supposedly thematic game is actively preventing me to get into the theme.


-> Rated a 10 from 6-3-13 to 27-3-13 to support Todd Breitenstein's fight against cancer. May he rest in peace.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
This is the game I really, really want to like, but it's just not very good. A large part of the problem is that the game sends mixed messages - it's competetive, in that there can only be one winner, but characters cannot actively hurt each other.

Zombies is a competetive game hiding in co-operative clothing. It uses tiles to build a board (I really like this facet of the game), dice to resolve combat (players can, to a degree, control combat using counters to influence their rolls, which I like), and cards to affect themselves and the other players.  It is these cards that I dislike, as they have a strong "take that" aspect to them, and are the primary means of interacting with other players, but only in a negative fashion.

Zombies lacks consistency, and suffers from poor pacing. I don't reccomend the game, but I really wish I could.

RATING: 10
I raised a zombie for Todd's cancer fight! Then I went out and got the game. It's the essential zombie apocalypse scenario with lots of room for house rules and customization. Great artwork, great with the not-a-regular-gamer crowd (especialy if they are into zombie flicks) and nicely priced too! I like it very much! It's simple and fun!

The only downside is the production wich feels kind of "cheap" compared to the competition but I see how higher production values would have raised the price.

The rating was to support Todd Breitenstein's fight against evil and as the game has grown on me since, I guess I'll leave it.

Just for the 100 zombie sculpts I would have given it a 10 anyway (1/10 zombies) ;)

RATING: N/A
Usually I play a game three times before rating. I don't need to in order to say that this game is the worst thing I have ever played, and an absolute waste of an hour and a half spent at the game night I was at before quitting halfway through. The game can be summarized by this: roll d6. That's it. Roll to kill zombies. Roll to move zombies. Roll to move character. Get interrupted by a game-breakingly powerful card, then look at your own hand of useless cards and feel powerless. And the game is breakable: Simply running around the map and never killing anything will allow you to place the helipad and win the game. I usually will stick through bad games, but there are no redeeming qualities here. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
What can I say that hasn't already been said? A fun game with a fun atmosphere that actually has a fair amount of depth provided by the event cards (you find that screwing with your friends becomes one of the most entertaining aspects of the game). Not suprisingly, one of the expansion sets consists solely of new event cards. The core rules are but a page or so in length, which can definitely be refreshing once in a while. One of the best, most fun, and most entertaining games I've ever played.

If you want a zombie-themed "beer and pretzels" game, you'll have much more fun with Zombie Dice. Same amount of fun as an entire game of Zombies!!!, but packed into 15 minutes, so it's much more enjoyable.

I rated this a '10' to try to boost its rating while Todd (the designer) was still fighting cancer, but once he passed away I reset it to what I really thought about the game.

RATING: 7
I bought this game way back when the 2nd edition dropped. I only recently started playing again after many life changes (marriage, college, kid, etc.). My feelings towards the game haven't changed much. It is a flawed but enjoyable game. 

The gripes I mainly see with this series are "it's too luck based" and "it's too simple." Both are mostly true, This is a very simple game, and much of the game is die roll and draw dependent. 

Winning/losing seems to be largely determined by the roll of the die and the luck of the draw. Except, I play with my wife, and I almost always win. It isn't due to great rolls and great draws, but rather the difference in how we play the cards we get and the decisions we make. I play aggressively, while she plays passively. This means, I take more risks, I play more "screw you" cards, I burn through cards as quickly as possible to always have access to new options, and I know which win condition to focus on given how the game is shaping up. This shows that even though it is a luck heavy game, the dice don't determine the winner/loser.

I find the game's simplicity to be more plus than a minus. Sometimes you want a hyper complicated game that requires as much mental energy and time investment as a full time job, But other times, you just want a simple, easy to set-up, quick, and enjoyable diversion... with zombies. This game is that. The simplicity issue gets fixed as you acquire more expansions, which add extra mechanics, variant ways to play, more cards, and individual player decks. 

Simplicity and the game's main flaw (vagueness) is also fixed by my favorite feature of board gaming. You are free and encouraged to tweak rules as you please. I love this. I have been playing video games my entire life and Yu-Gi-Oh (grudgingly) since it came stateside. These are fixed regulated experiences. You are at the mercy of the game, and you have no freedom to change things that don't work for you (unless you can use mods). Board games don't have this issue, and I love it. There are mechanics and cards I live and those I don't. I don't sue the stuff I don't like. I expand upon stuff I do like. Lately, we have been using the addictions and character card expansions as a base to create custom characters that fit our play. It adds to the game without changing it too much. We also use zombie animals where we see fit, like dogs or kids in town and bears in the woods. 

I would recommend this game to anyone into games, and if the enjoy it, I would recommend some of the expansions, especially 3.5 and 6 to expand the town, Deadtime Stories for lots of new content and ways to play, and later Defcon Z and the 2nd expansion to bring in a military base, infection, enhanced zombies, and more. I find the zoo and college expansions to be lackluster, but I love zombie animals, and the underutilized Guts Tokens offer a lot of great customized rule options.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

If it had been Uwe Rosenberg or Reiner Knizia, you stupid fuckers that complained about this wouldn't have bat an eye. The people that complained about this and got upset are an embarrassment to the hobby and I this Web site. So permanent 10, I hope others do the same to unnaturally raise this game's meaningless ranking.

The critical dichotomy that divides this game reminds me of the opinions I heard regarding ALIEN VS. PREDATOR.  "No plot", "stupid", "made no sense", "immature", "no character development"...WHAT THE HELL DID YOU PEOPLE EXPECT FROM A MOVIE CALLED "ALIEN VS. PREDATOR"?  Likewise, those who b*t*h and whine about this being a "dicefest" or "luck-driven" obviously don't get that ZOMBIES!!! is just supposed to be stupid, nonsensical fun geared toward horror movie fans.  You play it, you crack jokes, roll dice, and it doesn't really matter who wins.  Granted, if you try to play this with the beards-and-bellies set that likes to crunch numbers over a a game of El Grande this game is torture incarnate.  Play it with players who game to have fun rather than demonstrate their intellectual superiority via complex long term strategies and it's definitely an 8.  Plus it's fairly receptive to house rules, which cna really add to the good times.

RATING: 5.3
This game is worth a few laughs, but I'm not sure it's worth the cost to own it.  Players maneuver around a modular board, trying to slay 25 zombies, or make it to the helicopter, whichever comes first.  A simple roll of 4 or better on a die defeats a zombie.  The luck of the die and the attempts to push your luck by attacking "just one more" zombie leads to some amusing moments.

But there are several negatives.  First, the bullet and heart tokens are tiny, and hard to pick up off the tiles (which are themselves very thin).  Secondly, it's hard to move anywhere on the board quickly, making the potential strategy of going to pick up a key weapon you have listed on a card very difficult.  As you slog through to move just a couple boards, boards are added with still more zombies at an alarming rate.

This isn't a bad game, but it's just not the game for me - I'd rather play Last Night on Earth.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Picked this up at B&N while visiting Sheila in Greensboro and it started this whole obsessive game collection.

Out of the box, the game isn't much fun at all:  No one ever wants to go into any buildings (it's too easy to die), it sucks if you keep rolling poorly (especially for movement), and it's a waste of time placing tiles/zombies on every player's turn (since no one will ever even go to half of those tiles).

Still, a few house rules can make the game a lot better:  Only draw a new tile when you move near an edge, create custom characters that have set movement amounts and special skills, let weapon cards be used in any building, etc.

RATING: 6
This is an OK game that may be leaving my collection soon.  I like the tile laying mechanic along with each player controlling zombies each turn.  My main complaint is that it always ends up being an unnecessarily long game, especially since there are so many cards that give players the ability to prolong the ending by thwarting any "near victory" players plans.  The end game always ends up being just a race to the heliport with repeated "send back to start point" cards played along the way.  I would like it more except for that fact - it's too easy to make this game last far too long.

RATING: 4
I have never sold a game that I own before, but if/when I do, I will probably try to get rid of this one first.  

It takes way too long to play, there are almost no key decisions that you have to make, the board is constantly getting moved around due to the cheap nature of the board components and most of the game is spent moving zombies back and forth as you try to box in your opponent and they subsequently try to move them away so they can move.

It's one of those games you play when you first learn about board gaming, think it's amazing...and a few years later after you learn and play other games, realize that it really wasn't that good to begin with.

RATING: 10
This game is rated a 10 in honor of its designer, Todd Breitenstein, who lost his fight with cancer in 2013.  Although I am not particularly fond of the game itself (I would probably rate it at 5 or 6 in any other circumstance), this game will forever remain a 10, as well as a part of my revolving game collection, in his honor.  There are some things that are simply more important than any supposed "sanctity" of game ratings, and the fight against cancer is one of those things.  RIP, Todd, and know that you are not and shall never be forgotten.

RATING: 1
I've played this game twice, with different groups of people, and both times it ended with long-time close friends yelling at each other in anger. This game brings out the worst in people.

It's a dice-fest, and one bad roll can put you in a hopeless situation that just has you praying for the game to end.

Unfortunately, at the same time, someone else is having a great time and thinks it's a hoot. So each time he places new zombies onto the board, he places them in a way that is going to prolong the suffering of playing the game, even though there are other players begging -- PLEADING -- with him to just put everyone out of their misery.

Don't play this game with anyone you actually like.

RATING: 6
Zombies may suffer from some problems (such as rolling a die for movement) but when all is said and done, it's still good fun, if it doesn't go on too long. 
Witnessing a game unfold is like watching a movie, with subplots and missions unfolding, succeeding or failing, and new goals popping up... with players often working to achieve very different goals in very different ways. 

Plays  better with the expansions. 

I agree with others assessments that the game can go  on too long. There are numerous variants online (including here at BGG) that correct this problem. My rating reflects my opinions of the game "as is", out of the box with rules as written. If you get any one expansion, my recommendation would be the 3.5 cards expansion.

RATING: 4

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
This game is special because it renewed my interest in board games after my highschool/college days of playing Axis & Allies and Samurai Swords.  I thought it looked cool at a local hobby shop, and because of my purchase there, I was eventually led to BGG.

This is a take-that, player-screwage, type of game set in a zombie apocalypse.  Players explore a zombie infested city, flipping over one city tile at a time on their turn.  While doing so, players kill zombies and collect health and ammunition.  Players utilize cards to either give themselves benefits/equipment or use them on opponents to screw them over.  

The mayhem truly begins when the helicopter pad tile is drawn and everyone makes a mad dash to be the first player there.  Ultimately, there are no friends in Zombies!!!

The game is a little rough in the rules department and plays a bit long for what it is.  However, there is a lot of room for house-ruling and creating your own scenarios.  There aren't many deep decisions to be made and it is highly luck-dependent.  It's ok for what it is.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
RIP, Todd.


Brraaainnns....a simple game, given bonus points for the atmosphere...and *100 FRIGGIN' ZOMBIES!*

For a small publisher, this is certainly a great production.  You open the box and are immediately greeted with the little 100 plastic zombies.  The tiles are a decent thickness, the cards seem to handle wear well.

It's a roll and move affair with some cardplay, exploring the town, just trying to survive until the helipad turns up.  It's certainly thematic, but the rules are a bit rough, like it needs a bit more "there, there" for the length it takes to play.



EDIT:  This game needs house rules to help with bad endgame.  You think the end's in sight when the helipad comes up, but then whoa nelly does the cardplay come fast and furious.  Suddenly, everyone in town forgot to tie their shoelaces, or slipped, or hurt their leg, and of course the mad zombie congo line begins in earnest.

I dig this game, it just needs...help.

RATING: 10
Where do I begin with "Zombies!!!"?

I was introduced to Z!!! by a friend of mine many years ago. We played it hoping for an awesome Zombie game, what we got... was more than we bargained for.

Basically we played with 6 people, loved it, and even still to this day talk about how awesome it was. 

Now that I've moved away from those friends, I told myself I would buy Zombies!!! for myself, which I did.

Then I found out how many expansions there were for them!

Malls, Military Bases, Woods, Schools?? What!

So this game, is just fantastic. Build a city, collect items, battle your way through zombies, get to the chopper, win?

Such an easy game to learn, and so fun. It can be quick, or take the entire night to play.

And I can't wait to play it with expansions!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
“Good bad, I’m the guy with the gun.” -Ash

GAMEPLAY
A zombie thrashing game with simple roll and move turns and gotcha card playing. The goal of the game is to kill 25 zombies or reach the helicopter and live to tell the tale. The city is built each player turn as they are randomly laid from the stack. Each player takes it in turn to roll for movement fighting zombies along the way. Play cards with weapons on them to more effectively kill zombies or move faster. Other players play cards to add more zombies in your way. This game is a blast to play as you get stuck by your opponents. Unfortunately also because of this the game can drag on quite a long time. There are some house rules to help (check out the strategies).
COMPONENTS
The art is a generic modern city setting of good quality. The cards used for the city are too thin and need some back bending to flatten. Thicker stock would also help prevent the board shifting during gameplay. The models are about 15mm, there is a shotgun toting hero of six different colors and a bag full of zombies. You can and should augment your collection with a second bag purchased separately which will help for bigger games.
THEME
Everyone loves zombies! The simple mechanics and the unexpected twists and turns of the cards makes the game feel very cinematic and full of story. Brains…..
WHO IS IT FOR?
This is not a very deep game, with lots of dice rolling luck. That and the gotcha cards its hard to plan, there is chaos abound. Its tricky to recommend an age because of the subject matter, the game’s length is more of a factor try 12 and up. Games can be as short as 90 minutes but they can go on much longer.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[i]... dead walk the earth lightly and with much luck ... shell casings dance in hazy gore-spray ... send more cops ...[/i]

This rates a 5 played with the rules as written out of the box.  With the proper amount of house-rule spackle this can climb as high as a 7 or even an 8 with the right music, mood and people.

How much spackle?  [i]All of it.[/i]  You'll want to come up with new rules for movement, combat, endgame and victory conditions, using any combination of your own tasty brains, the [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/filepage/3063]Quick(er) Play Rules[/url], [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/user/Yugblad]Yugblad's[/url] suggestions:

[q=Yugblad]1. Throw out the rulebook.
2. Pick and choose from the variant rules on the Geek - remember to keep it SIMPLE!
3. Do not lay down tiles after finding the helipad.
4. Forget counting "dead" zombies for the winner - this is a kill-the-zombie-to-escape game. Let the most bloodthirst player place the helipad.
5. When a player dies, have him/her/them control the zombies, etc.
6. Trim the card deck to a custom-picked 50-60 cards. NO more, no less. Keep it 50/50 to screwage/benefit cards.
7. Use a timer - this keeps a panicky atmosphere ticking over.
8. Mount the town tiles on 2mm-thick card.
9. Use the subway expansion.[/q]
and the smorgasbord of rules salad on the Twilight Creations website.

I have to admit that I was very put off by this at first—if I wanted to make my own game I would have made my own game, not spent money on an unfinished product.  With time, however, I've very much warmed to the idea of [i]Zombies!!![/i] as a sandbox/toolkit experience game, a gaming hot rod that can be fiddled with and tuned until you get the custom ride that perfectly suits you & your game group.

If you dig the theme, have the time and are so inclined to tinker, this is pretty darn good.

:zombie:

My set-up:

[GAMEID=23972]
[GAMEID=31464]: glow-in-the-dark zombies, cards & tiles
[GAMEID=20494]: Guts tokens & cards
[GAMEID=28734]: Sewer tokens, cards & 3x subway tiles

(Donated to college games library.)

RATING: 6

RATING: 6
We've had a lot of fun playing this one.  Bad rolls can make the game tough (bad attack roles) or boring (bad movement roles) but there are a lot of "unofficial" rules to mitigate.  

[b]Something important that many don't seem to understand about this game[/b]: it is not about the players versus the horde of zombies, but rather the players versus each other... The zombies are just the death fodder you throw at each other.  

We've never had a problem with game length but have only ever played with 3 people and use a few house rules.

If someone were to look at my game shelf and ask to play this, I'd suggest we play [GameID=7514] instead as it's probably more along the lines of what they're looking for.

EDIT: Original rating of 6, [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/940650/important-show-some-real-community-support]temporarily giving a rating of 10[/url].

2013-05-21

Inital Rating: 8.0 (January 2011)

Zombies!!! Was one of the first zombies` game I ever bought and played (I have 3 unplayed expansions for this). I love that it comes with many miniatures, however the gameplay lacks in many ways. It has a ton of luck, almost no strategy and the “attack the leader” effect guarantees that the game will take a long playtime.  

On the good side the game components are pretty cool.

I believe there are a lot of good variants that can be played with this marvelous components. Still I don’t want to get rid of my copy, in fact I still want to buy all the expansions! But this is not a good game by itself. I want to play it once every two years.

Current Rating: 4.0
[hr]
2015-02-02

I finally played Zombies!!! Again and i would rate it higher if the playtime wasn’t so long for what the game offers. I think I have finally moved on so I can get rid of my copy of the game, it saddens me a bit to sell it because I really dig the miniatures, however the heart and bullet tokens are very regular but I really like the art.

I’m not sure if I want to try the unplayed expansions, we will see what happens but, either way, Zombies!!! is in its way out of my game collection, now it is just a matter of time.

Current Rating. 4.0

I made a few minor changes to the rules by mistake (nothing affecting play too much actually) that ended up speeding up the game and made some weapons wicked fun.

I'm not sure that the whole series is worth the money, but if you enjoy the game and play it a fair ammount I'd want them for diversity if nothing else.

RATING: 10
R.I.P. Todd.

 Zombies was a great buy when it first came out and still is. There are other games that have surpassed it gameplay wise but not many have surpassed it in the bang for your buck department.

If played with some of the variant rules it really is a decent game and it really does deserve it's place in the history of gaming. 

What follows are my original comments.

I haven't actually played using the rules that come with the game. Drops a point if I do. There are plenty of variants out there and scenarios so you can find a game here that you will like if your any kind of zombie fan at all. Buy the game, download some variants and enjoy.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
I have a soft spot for this game, because this is the game that introduced me to the world of board gaming. A few years ago a game shop opened in my city, and I saw this zombie game. Loving zombies, I decided to give it a try. Before this game I had never even heard of a game with a modular board, so you can imagine my surprise. I remember thinking, "Why isn't this more common?! This is great!" And that lead me to search for modular board games, and that lead me to Carcassonne and that lead me here. Life has never been the same, ha.

Weight: Light
Audience: Horror fans, fans of zombies (title didn't give that away, did it?)
Number of players: 2-6.
Components: They're pretty good. The map tiles are thin. They're made of a durable glossy paper and not cardboard, but they're of good quality. The hearts and bullet tokens (of which there are many, all of them are tiny) could have perhaps been better outlined on a kind of character sheet or card, but that may not have really worked with the nature of how simple this game is intended to be.
Rules: Simple. 
Setup: Very quick.
Game-flow: This game can perhaps drag on if played by the rules that come in the box, but Twilight Creations website, as well as the Geek, can fix that issue for you with an abundance of altered rules and variants.
Randomness: High.
Player interaction: Mid to low.
Fun: Depending on the mood and group, I could rate this game anywhere from 3 up to 6.
Theme: Works for me. Zombies are everywhere, and you're running around an unfamiliar city!
Recommended to: See Audience.

RATING: 2
Thanks for this one Todd! You brought a lot of joy to some of my friends and for that I'm very thankful.

Played twice. I won't ever play again if I can avoid it. 100% pure luck, long, and mostly boring although some screwage cards can elicit a laugh or two now and then. Production is mixed. You get some soft plastic figs. The board is made up of thin cardboard tiles that lack any sort of variety unless it's a 'named' location (Fire Station, Gas Station, Sports Store, etc) so it mostly looks boring and nothing like a city once the tiles are layed out, but more like a maze. Would have been better to keep the zombies but make it a hedge maze or dungeon, at least it'd make more sense. If the game play was anything other than luck with a few screwage cards, the production wouldn't matter at all.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
LOTS of fun, despite the vague instructions. We had to refer to FAQ's and join the Zombies!!! yahoo forum to search out unanswered questions in he small manual, and there's still a number of situations that may come up in this game that will leave us wondering what to do. As the game builds, the zombie infestation increase; you can run, but not for long as your opponents will use their cards and move the Zombies around to wreak all kinds of havoc in your path -- (of course, you'll be doing the same). Depending on your goal, slicing and dicing through hordes of zombies can be a good or bad thing. Do you go for zombie kill count, or race for the heli-pad for a quick escape. Oh wait, the helipad isn't present yet - where on the board will it appear...?

Lots of plastic zombies in the second edition, (2 bags..grey/green - even Zombie Gals). The ghoulishly-funny card illustrations are excellent, as are the map tiles; what I wasn't happy with were the bullet and life heart punch outs which are very tiny, making them a bit annoying to handle and place on a map card. Get a group together and let those Zombies 'Have Some'. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 1
The rulebook should have clued me in - whenever a game has using house rules that are commonly accepted it typically means that the game itself is already broken. When a game ENCOURAGES IT IN THE RULEBOOK gravely ill omens have been marked, for here there be garbage. 

If this game wasn't about zombies it would be nearly universally despised and people would never play it. This is a horrible game - maybe the worst game I've ever played. 

The game's draw mechanic is inherently broken. Many of the game's cards are "take that!" cards that seriously hamstring one's opponents - and since there is no penalty for playing as many cards as possible (since one can always draw up to full). This would be fine, if ...

combat wasn't so utterly broken and agonizing. There are a few cards in the deck that make combat actually viable - but since most of the game's meat de facto is trying to screw one's neighbors they are seldom seen and rarely able to be used. Players are guaranteed to die many, many times, which puts them very close to square one and utterly qipes out what progress they have made. Since this happens to everyone the game quickly falls into frustration until ...

the tile for the Helipad is drawn. But even this action, which would mercifully end the game, can be wrecked by virtually any player. This game goes on forever and ever, and I've played more than one game that has just ended with attrition to watch Road House or something.

I've left out other critical problems such as the roll-and-move mechanic, the pointless tiny chits when a cardboard character sheet would be far more practical - but this game is already a miserable enough experience without them. There are no meaningful decisions to be made, the dice determine far too much of what happens in the game, and ever action in this game is much more akin to what would make one lose least as opposed to gain most. The game's bits aren't bad (except for the tiny chits) - I've met more than one person who has considered buying the game _because a good game can be made in it somewhere_. That says something. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Great graphics and theme with appealing horde of 100 zombies to play with.  Competition to win is ruthless, with most cards being used to screw your opponents and can be played at any time to thwart their strategies.  My only complaints are the life & bullet tokens which are small, fiddly & similar, and the fact that the game goes on a bit too long - this can be changed by removing a few city tiles but it seems a shame to do so.  We played with 6 players and it was tedious, 2 or 3 was about right.  Expansion pack of cards 3.5 adds to game play.  All other expansions are optional.  The game has lots of fun scenarios (such as 'pizza delivery') at the manufacturers website: http://www.twilightcreationsinc.com/zombies/

RATING: 6
Silly dicefest with a lot of zombies. Surprisingly high component quality considering the game's price. Way too long for what it is though, but it scratches a very particular itch thanks to its dead simple nature, making it worth playing on carefully selected occasions. 

On the one hand, if you want a remotely deep game, don't even dare touching it. Consider fleeing to another country if you are being pressed into it. And if that doesn't work, set yourself ablaze. It'll probably be less painful than enduring a whole gaming session.
Rating: :nostar::nostar::nostar::nostar::nostar:

On the other hand, if you have a really silly day, it's perfect. You know, one of those days when you don't want to give things a second thought. When all you want to do is rolling dice. When your decisions are taken because "Zombie conga line! LOL!". All while simultaneously rambling about life, the universe and everything. If you are having one of these days, then [i]Zombies!!![/i] is just THE GAME. Specially when playing with the "mandatory bowls of chips and cold refreshments" variant. 
Rating: :star::star::star::star::star::star: 

Yes, those are six stars. "But Luis, you rate games on a one to five scale scale! This is silly". F**k that! Star conga line!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
I'm not at all certain why this game is so popular. The art is not bad, the gameplay is a bit sluggish and the strategy is, well, not very present. Die rolls and card draws rule the game, and there's a lot of moving bits around that don't need to be moved. Also, playing takes too long for what it is, much like the more recent Twilight Creations game, "Dante's Inferno".

The theme is fun and any game where you use a grenade to blow up a toy store full of the walking dead can't be all bad, but this one just ambles by, dropping stinky chunks as it goes.

The suggested rules found on this website would improve the game considerably - my gaming group doesn't want to play the game again with the rules as they exist. 

Two parting shots - do some proofreading on the rulesheet and cards, please - it's not like there are a lot of them. Secondly, NEXT time, make the bullet and life counters look a little different, for goodness sake. Reverse the black and white, put a little letter on them, colour one red - anything! Just make it easier to tell them apart at a glance.

RATING: 1
Someone once described Zombies!!! to me as "The perfect template to make a great game". The components are great, the tiles and figurines can be used for many games, ...

Unfortunately the actual game is horrible. And your turn if you get a 1 on the dice, you will only move once, which means you will do almost nothing on your turn, while someone getting a 6 will get weapons, kill lot of zombies, etc...

After that, it gets even worse, with the dreaded "Munchkin ending". If people are used to boardgame, then everyone will block everyone else for 1 or 2 hours, a few tiles away from the helicopter through the play of "screw you" cards. Then, finally someone will be lucky enough to get a good enough roll, and none of his opponents will have bad cards to stop him, and this game will finally ends.

At the end of the day, it's based too much on luck to be a staple game that I break out frequently.

RATING: 3
70% of map generally remains unused which is a huge bummer.  Venturing into buildings for bullets/hearts is nearly always a losing gamble if you take the initiative (clean up after another player for the win though).  Building-Specific cards are nearly useless given how large the map is when actually played out.  Not much strategy other than to make a dash for the chopper or to know when to "strategically die" in order to restart with your 3/3 count.  Trying to accumulate 25 kills is damn near impossible and almost certainly leads to players dashing for the chopper as the winning strategy.

Suggested house rules or updates: [1] Building cards can be played in any building (chainsaw, skateboard, etc.), [2.] Either kill limit is shortened to 15 zombies, or a winning dice roll is three and higher (for a 2/3rds chance of combat wins rather than 1/2 chance).

RATING: 7
Una buena estrategia inicial (aunque es un juego de dados y por tanto de mucho y voluble azar) puede ser la siguiente:

1. En los primeros compases del juego y mientras no aparezca la ficha de Helipuerto, cuando toque mover zombies en tu turno, hacerlo de manera que se alejen todo lo posible de los rivales, de manera que éstos, si quieren matar zombies o entran en edificios o deben sacar tiradas de dados altas, lo que dificulta su "recolección" de zombies. 
Cuando aparezca la casilla de Helipuerto hacer todo lo contrario  y llenar el camino de zombies para ralentizar la llegada de los rivales al helicóptero.

2. Colocar las fichas de calle de forma que cuando esté cerca la posibilidad de salida del Helipuerto (cuando se haya colocado en juego la mitad del mazo de las fichas de calles, esto es, 14 fichas de terreno), esta casilla no pueda ponerse demasiado cerca de donde se encuentran los rivales y en cambio se coloque lo más cerca posible de ti; esto aumenta la posibilidad de que seas tú el que huya en helicóptero y gane la partida.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Way back when, this was one of the best zombie games around, because it was one of the only zombie games around. Now, it shows its age.

You win by either killing 25 zombies (tough, as combat is a rarely-modifiable dice roll, and your death cuts your current kill count in half) or being the first to the helipad, which is stacked at the bottom of the location tile stack.

Most games are decided by the helipad, which means milling around for 30 - 45 minutes waiting for it to hit the table, all the while stocking up on as many screw-you cards as possible. The end condition resembles Kill Dr Lucky's design and Munchkin's functional end state, where the winner is the player whose turn comes after the guy who soaked up all the stopper cards.

RATING: 6
You and the other players are in the middle of a city overrun by the living dead. Your goal is to slay 25 zombies or reach safety at the helipad. Cards are used to help your mission or muck up other players' plans. Each turn you place a new city block tile, move your character and move a random number of zombies (usually to harass the other players). It's a fun beer and pretzels game.

RATING: 2
1 / 5 - Bad.

This should be a fast-playing action game, but it isn't, at least not with five players like I tried it. Having to dig tokens and figures out of the box each time a tile is laid makes downtime a real pain with this one - all the more so since if you roll poorly for movement on your turn you're effectively doing nothing anyway, making things drag further. Has a nasty tendency to extend its play time past the welcome stage as well and it looks like the winner is often going to be the one who places the helipad. This might be more fun with 2 or 3 players but I can't say I'm inspired enough to bother finding out.

RATING: 2
There is a popular move to rate this game a 10 in order to support the designer, who is battling the advanced stages of cancer:  http://boardgamegeek.com/thread/940650/important-show-some-real-community-support 

I show my support for this cause by not reflecting my honest opinion in the BGG ratings.  I found the game dragged in the early and mid game, and our group deliberately cut the tile deck in order to hasten the end.  Only once the helipad tile appeared did the game get more interesting and focused - otherwise it was largely aimless shambling.  I wouldn't play it again if asked.  

But I wish the designer and those close to him all the best during what must be a terribly difficult time.

Oct 2014: time has passed and time to rate the game for how I feel about it.

Do not expect some giocone the year. Zombies! Second Edition is a game that enjoys a great setting, an exceptionally high visual impact, but at the same time bit more fun that the complex game mechanics. What if one side can make up their noses to the hardcore gamer, you may reveal a winning move for the identification, referring to the frenzy, speed and immediacy that a situation would result. Exactly offset by the material really well made and attractive and can add value with its numerous expansions!

RATING: 4
After one play (2-player game), I am fairly unimpressed. The idea is neat, and some of the cards are fun, but the end game is long and got quite tedious in our session. Each of us died at least a couple times within just a few squares of the helipad. A few of the rules are silly, and a few of the cards are vague about implementation. I'd prefer tiles that were a little thicker, as the thin, glossy stock makes them slide around too much. The minis don't do anything for me. I'm a hex and counter guy from back in the day, and so it made no difference to me to push minis rather than chits. Getting screwed and sent back to the town square or put in an impossible situation was fun but only up to a point. After a while, it just got aggravating. We got some laughs, but I think we got even more frustration. I would be willing to play a 3- or 4-player game to see how that goes.

Not even if this were substantially shorter would it be the answer to the most important question of our age: "What is the zombie game that doesn't suck?"

RATING: 10
This game will always stay in my collection. It has great components at a fantastic price and it is so imminently hackable. If you are a game designer, you should have this game in your collection and look at all the ways you can make it your own.

But that doesn't mean you have to change anything. I play this game with my cousins and we have a blast screwing each other up every time we play. The constant struggle against each other is standard Zombie movie fair and we love all the amazing homegrown variants and scenarios. 

This is a game that is too often written off, but the point of games is to play them for fun and I've had a ton of fun playing this game.

RATING: 7
Fast paced and frantic! It's Resident Evil in board game form as players unveil a city teeming with undead zombies and must either battle their way to the landing pad and hop onto the last chopper out, or kill 25 zombies! A fun "not-too-much-thinking" game that's hard to resist, especially if you like the theme and genre. Bonus for no elimination. House rules and variants are encouraged and probably a good idea as this game can take a long time when played out of the box.

RATING: 4.5
+ .5 can give you an "i'm kicking ass" feeling -  helped by the fact this game includes 100s of miniatures ... but only if you're not inclined to think too hard (or are drunk) -

+ .5 plenty of 'gotcha!' elements that can work somewhat well for competitive versions with the right group/setting... but also has the 'everyone destroys the person in the lead' side-effect, with no mitigating design choices. 

+ .5 collaborative mode can work and be enjoyable... but this can make a lot of the aspects of the game redundant or like a slog. 


-2 overall, just broadly shallow on strategy and mechanics once you get past the core mechanic of mowing down zombies. 


Fun for when people are drunk but still want to play a boardgame.

RATING: 2.5
This game has become too old. The manual should have been polished during all those years, it still leaves some things unclear.

The endgame conditions are way too difficult. It says it lasts 60 minutes... My games always lasted more than double that ammount. After the first half an hour, I become bored of doing the same over and over and not having any progress done, and I just wish for the game to end.

The game is too random, and there are too many "take that" cards, one player will finally win because he will find himself in a position to use one of his cards to win (by chance or because the other players just want the game to finish :p).

75% of the event cards will be usless (there's only one weapon really useful).

I can think of much better games to play. I will do my best to avoid playing this one again.

RATING: 6
This is a great beer and pretzels game. Needs some house rules to tighten it up though.
1. Movement is still 1d6 but you always roll at least your health. So if you have 3 health you round up anything less than 3 up to 3.
2. Instead of placing a tile at the start of turn. Players have to actually explore new tiles. Players can see up to 1 tile away as long as line of sight exists and they're not in combat with a zombie.
3. When you die you place a zombie on the nearest empty space.

RATING: 6
Fun idea, especially with the plastic zombie figures and tiles that allow players to set up a different game each time they play. No great shakes in design, compared to more contemporary games, but very good in its time, and still can be fun, but more likely so if one limits the size of the draw deck, to keep the game reasonably short. I like the plastic zombie figures and the human toting shotguns, and the artwork on the events cards is a hoot. I do think it's a design that verily invites variations, as many have suggested on BGG. My 10-year-old rated it an 8.5 (July 2009) and after his first play, he and I started sharing ideas for how to add our own variations to certain rules. After a few more plays (August 2009), he bumped his rating up to 9.5. Finally, I also think it's one of those games that one has to bring one's own passion to; otherwise it would seem slow to play and dull by comparison with other games, especially more recent games. Personally, I like to use the rule which allows players to randomly insert the helicopter pad tile into the bottom half of the (28-tile) stack, to speed things up, as there's not enough to the game play itself to justify a longer game, and there's too much of a feeling of doing the same thing over and over, which tends to drag down the enjoyment. Plus the sheer number of player-inspired rules variations indicates a design that came up short, even though it's also a franchise game. Purchased used, October 2008.

RATING: 1.5
Zombies!!! is a 30 minute game that takes 3 hours to play. 

The theme makes no sense - why are the humans trying to screw each other over - surely they should be working together? And the theme is the only thing this game has going for it! 

It is roll and move, has cards that say things like 'miss a turn' or 'go back to the start.' Fighting is done by rolling dice. It is one of those games that never terminates because everyone plays 'bash the leader' cards when someone is about to win, until either everyone runs out of cards and someone manages to win, or you give up in frustration.

Truly dreadful.

It would be useable as a game for young children, except the gory artwork is unsuitable.

Maybe we could make a new game out of the components in the box. 

I ended up posting my copy to a trade scammer who never posted anything in return. 

My copy was stolen by a trader scam.

RATING: 5
If you are worried about running long, just take out some cards/decrease the # of zombies needed to win. I did this, cut the cards to 6 per person in a 3 player game and put the chopper in last 4. Also decreased kill target to 15/20 (vs. 25) and it made it a fairly quick and enjoyable 3p game.

Shortened games of this are key. That's important here. 

Fun for awhile, but I have since poached the zombies for other games, and the box for Mogul.

RATING: 6
Un gioco senza pretese, ma divertente (e con ottimi componenti). Raggiunge la sufficienza per almeno tre motivi:
1. L'ambientazione: il sottoscritto ha un debole per gli zombi. Ogni pezzo del gioco (carte, edifici, situazioni, anche lo scopo del gioco) è si ispira a una delle cento pellicole dove sono protagonisti.
2. L'ironia: tutto, dalle istruzioni alle carte azione, ne è pervaso. Meglio di un gioco sugli zombi c'è un gioco sugli zombi (auto)ironico.
3. L'interazione tra giocatori: tutti si mettono i bastoni tra le ruote. Le coltellate migliori si danno quando esce la tessera finale.
E poi è semplicissimo quel tanto che basta per coinvolgere anche amici a digiuno di boardgame.

RATING: 4
Rating Change:  After years of owning Zombies!!! and many plays, I've decided that I simply do not like the game.  I tried, I really did, but the combination of clunky rules (1d6 movement can often leave you with nothing to do on your turn save for taking a couple of uneventful steps through empty tiles), 50/50 combat and extreme downtime in a six player game just makes the whole thing an exercise in tedium for me.  Whenever it hits the table it's sort of fun for the first couple of rounds and then it just gets stale fast.  It's also one of the few games I know of where the guy in last place has the best chance of winning, and how can that ever be a good thing?  Bleh, I'll bring Last Night on Earth to the table before this game every time now.

Crossing the Bar
By Alfred, Lord Tennyson

Sunset and evening star,
      And one clear call for me!
And may there be no moaning of the bar,
      When I put out to sea,

   But such a tide as moving seems asleep,
      Too full for sound and foam,
When that which drew from out the boundless deep
      Turns again home.

   Twilight and evening bell,
      And after that the dark!
And may there be no sadness of farewell,
      When I embark;

   For tho' from out our bourne of Time and Place
      The flood may bear me far,
I hope to see my Pilot face to face
      When I have crost the bar.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7

Straight out of the box the game is clunky and counter intuitive so time is well spent altering the rules to your liking. By all means play the game with its original rules to get a feel of how the game was intended but I'm sure you'll want to make changes early on.

Zombies!!! is fun, especially when you manage to totally screw over another player and laugh as they fall foul to the undead :) The random board generation works in its favour but can take up a lot of space so make sure you have a big table or play on the floor. The book keeping can get pretty tiresome after a while (placing zombies, ammo, bullets every turn) but this can be counteracted once players know the game well and agree to play really quickly. Playing quickly is a necessity especially if you're playing with an expansion + the core set, otherwise the game will get bogged down and go on all night.

I'm giving Zombies!!! a 7 because although it's a good, fun game its flaws are many and patently obvious to the degree that one wonders how such oversights made it to production.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.8
I love the expanding map mechanic on a turn-by-turn basis.  Love, love, love, love, love it.  Love it.  I also greatly enjoy a game based solely on screwing your opponent.  It's a welcome change of pace on occasion.  Unfortunately, once the map reaches a certain size (especially once the helipad comes out), the map building mechanic loses every single bit of attraction.  The game stops being about killing zombies and exploring the map segments, and it becomes entirely about making a mad dash for the helipad.  Often times we won't even place zombies on the tiles that come out after the helipad, as they are entirely obsolete.  Why would a person run to the opposite side of the map just to slay some more zombies or grab more ammo and health when the endgame is right there?  Also, there are several occasions in which you'll have a great item you'd love to use, but you can't because the building that it requires has not yet been produced on the map.  Zombies!!! is a fun diversion, but a deeply flawed game.

RATING: 6
A good beer & pretzels kind of game. Roll the dice, kill some zombies, screw your buddy. It's simple, it's fun. There are a lot of opportunities for big moments, with players completely surrounded and yet still finding their way to safety (or going down in a blaze of glory).

I prefer this game without any of its (numerous) expansions. While adding extra mechanics and locations to most games is fun, this game works well because it is so simple.

That said, I would suggest trying a game or two of Zombies!!! combined with the Humans!!! spin-off; some players play as zombies instead of survivors, and each player has a unique goal. It changes things up in an interesting way, and while the zombie players have a few more rules they need to know, anyone can still opt to play as a survivor, keeping the game about as simple for them as it was before.

RATING: 2
I'd read this was a lame game, and it is indeed the most disappointing game I've played in a long time.  Vague parts in the rules, ambiguous confusing map tile art (another triumph of cool art over functionality), but worst of all it has very little excitement and doesn't really capture the feel of a zombie horror film.  It's more like a tedious repetitive dice fest that drags on forever.  Your randomly rolled movement points each turn are too few, so it takes forever to move around the map.  It dragged on and on, and we eventually got too tired to continue and just went to sleep.  The game box doesn't tell how long the game takes, and I wonder if it's because they don't know because no one ever finished a game.

A hundred plastic zombies are a fun idea, but it feels like that was the core idea of the game, and the rules were just slapped together to have an excuse to sell a hundred plastic zombies in a box.

It was also annoyingly inconvenient that the life and bullet counters are printed only one one side (red life, black bullets) with indistinguishably identical white backs.  They get moved around and accidentally flipped over a lot, so they really should have been printed on both sides.
 
The 2-player card game Zombiaki is playable in less than half an hour and much better captures the feel of a zombie film.

=== 

Meanwhile the game has a bogus misleading high rating with roughly a thousand people "temporarily" rating it "10" due to [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/940650]a campaign in March 2013 to raise its rating as high as possible[/url] (and people like me who had rated it low even received direct geekmails pressuring them to change their rating).

Despite this "10" campaign being "temporary" with people supposed to restore their honest ratings soon thereafter, most of those "10" ratings still remain, years later.

RATING: 6
13-01-2015. Rated after 1 play. I may have played Zombies!!! over 10 years ago, but I forgot. Zombies!!! is a classic game about Escaping from bunch of Zombies!!! in a city by being the first to kill 20 zombies, or empty and reach the helipad first. 

The game starts with all players on a deserted town square. Each turn, you roll a d6 for movement and move through the city, playing cards to help yourself or screw your opponents. New tiles are revealed and placed when you move off a tile you're at. On the tiles is listed how many Zombies you spawn, how many bullits and hearts there are. 

Combat is dead easy and happens each time you are in the same location as a zombie. You roll a die, if you roll a 4+, you kill the zombie. If you roll less than 4, you can discard bullets to get a +1 on your roll. If you don't manage, you lose a lifepoint (heart). If you ever lose all your life you respawn at the city center, but lose half your zombies.

Zombies is, like I said, a classic. I am not sure if time has been kind to it. The game is an ultra light, take-that kind of screw your buddy game. It's fun though, although it can run a little long. I prefer this to Munchkin.

RATING: 2.7
The game is simple enough: roll dice to move and kill zombies, and either whoever kills 25 zombies first or reaches the helipad first wins. Unfortunately, the simplicity is in no way an enhancement to the experience of playing. The only enjoyable aspect I can see in the game is getting into the role-playing idea of being in a zombie apocalypse, which is helped a lot by the clever animations on the cards and tiles. Still, this by no means offsets the unnecessary length of each game (seriously, an average 4 player game takes longer than any zombie movie I know of) nor the repetitive gameplay, which pretty much consists of killing zombies and trying to find uses for the cards. The worst part of the game is when the helipad is revealed because the game naturally devolves into a "go after the person winning" strategy which involves all the other players unleashing all their bitch-move cards on the near-winner; usually this continues until someone kills 25 zombies (which, considering the 50% chance dice rolls, takes a VERY long time...) Do yourself a favor and play "Last Night On Earth" - you won't regret it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.75
Played this one a few times, and it ends up being fun every time. 

The mechanics are far from sound. Games mostly comprise a lot of chaotic running around and random tile-laying. It's thus far worked out that the bravest player has been the winner.

I think there are perhaps too many tiles in the standard deck. It doesn't take long before the board is so overrun with zombies that there's no way you'll reach the new tiles, even if you wanted to (which you probably wouldn't).

In the future, I'll look into existing variants, to try to balance some of the chaos.

RATING: 2
I really don't like this game at all, but since many people enjoy it I will expand upon my low rating. As always, it's just my opinion and the game may work for your group. To the scathing criticism, then...

The phases of a turn in Zombies are as follows: 

1) draw random event cards if needed 
2) place a random tile 
3) roll d6 to move, battling zombies en route by rolling a d6 (it doesn't matter which direction you move, since the direction of your destination -- the helipad -- is unknown until the final tile is placed)
4) roll a d6 to move the undead (and it doesn't matter much where you move them, since the other players can move them as as well)
 
At some point in the turn you may play / discard / activate event cards. 

It should be apparent from the turn description above that the only real choices in the game are which cards to play and which to discard; literally everything except the card play rests on a strong random element. Sadly, the cards themselves are unbalanced, and when combined with the roll-and-move mechanism, give the game the feel of Snakes and Ladders. Sample cards include 'go back to the start' and 'advance ten spaces'. On top of this, the rules are poorly written and ambiguous. On the upside, the bits are plentiful and of good quality. As Tom Vasel -- or someone -- says, I'm sure there's a great game that can be made with the supplied bits, but the one described in the rulebook ain't it. 

If you manage to massage the rules into shape (probably with the QuickPlay rules from BGG), 3 or 4 is a more accurate rating.

Like Carcassonne, Zombies plays better with few or no expansions and maybe 3 or 4 players. If you go overboard on the players and / or expansions, the game can really drag on -- one 5P game with the Mall Walkers expansion took us 3.5 hours.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Poor design. The expansions are overpriced and generally don't add a lot (I have the mall).  There's a soft spot in my heart for this game because of the evocative card artwork, but I wish it was more than it is.

RATING: 5

An additional suggestion would be to make it 3-6 to kill Zombies. This makes the game move along at a faster clip and makes zombie killing a more viable strategy.

RATING: 3
Totally not as bad as it should be.  It is thematically entertaining, and it works well for what it is.  It doesn't feel like just another take that card game.  But there isn't much here other than roaming around and rolling dice.

The grinding through all the same zombies does get monotonous and getting around the map takes forever.  Often the cards limit your movement, have other players return you to a dead end or cause you to lose a turn.  I think a game that injects friction on that level is suffering from a weak design.  Were it not for this it still only would rate a 4, but losing a turn (possibly multiple turns) or having your actions undone is so obnoxious that I'm dropping the rating by a point.

The Zombie figs are awesome though.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
[b]"It's a No Brainer!"[/b] Just like it says on the box or it could say, [b]"Just Luck!"[/b]

There are only two options hope you get lucky with lots of good rolls killing zombies. Lots of good rolls=25 good rolls.

Or...

Stay in last place, so you can place the Helipad near you to win.

[b]The most winning strategy is staying in last place? Yep.[/b]

If you have the cards [i]The Keys Are Still In It[/i] and [i]Alternate Food Source[/i], just wait by whoever is in last place (hopefully you) for the helipad and victory to show up.

RATING: 3

The nub of the problem is that you can never feel that you are making any progress toward a goal or even making decisions that might have some effect on the outcome -- why go down one street rather than another, and why shuffle around zombies here rather than there? You can't even hope for a few lucky rolls that will provide a quick escape from the tedium.

RATING: 4
This game is just all random dice rolls.  On your turn you place a tile and place elements on that tile.  Zombies, hearts (which represent your life and let you re-roll), and bullets (which let you add 1 to a roll).  Then you roll to move and subsequently roll to defeat any zombies you encounter with a 50/50 shot.

Very.  Boring.  The game does have items that let you move extra spaces or hit harder in combat or even hinder your opponents.  The win condition is a race to either get to the helipad or kill 25 zombies.  There are so many zombie horde killing games out there that do what this game tries to do so, so much better that you can pretty much ignore this one.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5.9
Use shorter game rules: The chopper is shuffled into the bottom half of the deck. The person with the least ammount of Zombies places the chopper. After chopper out, roll 2 die for movement. Other Variants: Movement = life tokens + 2. If you end your movement on the center of Town Square, you can fill up to 3 lives and 3 bullets. You always move 3 zombies at the end of your turn. Your movement is doubled if Helipad is on the table.

RATING: 3
Players place a map tile, spawn zombies, roll to move then roll to move the walking dead, attempting to either reach the helipad (once it's placed) or kill 25 zombies. The elevator pitch is "take-that zombie dicefest". There's a certainly a lot of take that, in the form of cards that either help you or ruin other players' chances, but the luck factor is overwhelming.

As a game, it embodies all that is wrong with the "Ameritrash" school of design; as an activity you can get some laughs out of it.

RATING: 3
The basic premise behind this game holds potential, but in the end the mechanics just don't create a very fun experience.  Essentially the game boils down to a LOT of roll and move/kill and any potential for strategy is stripped away.  I suppose with the right people this game can be fun in a beer and pretzels sort of way, but I have a habit of gaming sober, so it doesn't do much for me.  Others have suggested house rules to spice things up and add some strategy.  I haven't explored those possibilities enough to see if they have merit, but I also haven't been motivated enough to do so.  Ultimately I see this as a game that just isn't that good.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
You would need to be a zombie to enjoy this game. Move, roll some dice, get shafted by a card, go back to square one. Repeat ad nauseum. It's one of those tedious "bash the leader" affairs which manages to eke out the game needlessly for the whole evening until you are praying for the game to end. The roll and move mechanic is incredibly dated and tedious. Imagine waiting 5 minutes for your turn to come round only to end up rolling a 1 for your move. Oh well, doesn't matter anyway because another played a card that means you have to miss a turn so may as well sit back and watch the "hilarity" unfold. This might be a fun beer and pretzels game if it didn't drag on for quite so long, and the fact that the first half of the game is spent wandering aimlessly around the map waiting for the helipad to appear. While the theme is great on paper, the game completely fails to capture any of the tension or pathos of the great zombie movies. 

Gave away to charity.

RATING: 3.5
Sometimes you go in to a game knowing that you're not going to enjoy it. I've played *a lot* of games in the past few years, but not this one so when it was suggested recently, I agreed, albeit with very, very low expectations.

The map building aspects are pretty underwhelming. Draw a tile and place a tile. The movement is the roll of a D6. Combat is a 50/50 chance. It was apparent as early as my first turn that the best thing to do was to stay still and hope that everybody else died trying to kill 25 zombies.

2 hours later, 2 people had died and 4 of us were slowly working our way to the helipad. Of course, with 14 or so zombies on the three or so tile spaces blocking access to the helipad it was essentially a matter of who decided to suicide themselves on the horde so the others might be able to get through. Let's just pause here to remind ourselves that this IS NOT a co-operative game. Two of the players decided to work as a team and do whatever they could to make sure one of the two of us won. It was the most sensible thing to do and prevented the game running for any longer than it already had.

RATING: 1
Brutal. Not a round went by without me going "What was the designer thinking?"

First, the goals in this game are almost opposite of what they should be. It's a competitive game and feels more like Deer Hunter than zombie survival. You win by either killing 25 zombies first or reaching the helipad. Since reaching the helipad is almost entirely dominated by luck (whoever is closest to where it's placed has a huge advantage), the strategy is basically "open season on zombies". Yes, you actually want to actively go after and hunt down the zombies. You get to roll for both your player movement and zombie movement, and it's not uncommon to make the zombies attack yourself for more chances to get points (zombie kills). This would be OK if the theme was more like a comedy zombie scenario (i.e. Zombieland or Sean of the Dead), but it's tailored to be horror. Yes, oh no, you spawned a bunch of zombies in the building I'm in, I'm horrified... free points!

I guess there can theoretically be a point in time where strategy comes into play and someone could be wanting to run away and get supplies rather than fight zombies, so then you could hinder instead of help them. Probably as you reach the ridiculous amount of 25 zombies needed is when this would become more prominent (as you lose half if you die). There's also a lot of goofy "take that" action cards that simply remove someone's zombie cache and puts them back into play which don't help the game at all from a fun/strategy perspective.

The tiles you reveal are bland, which isn't helped by the location-based action cards almost never working or being worth it. The other actions are "take that", which is almost the only form of player interaction because the "now you get to attack other players with zombie" phase is actually the "move zombies closer to you so you can kill them first" phase. Turns take forever because of the ridiculous tile/hit/bullet/zombie placement.

I had more fun trying to stack the zombie miniatures than I did playing the actual game. Avoid like the plague!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
A simple game where players are people trapped in a town full of zombies. First to make it to the heliport or kill 25 zombies wins. Cards are used to represent events in the game such as finding weapons or zombies. Simple counters are used to keep track of certain aspects of the game. The game comes with 100 little zombie miniatures. Category: Exploration, Horror, Fighting, Miniatures, Movies/TV/Radio theme;  Mechanics: Modular Board, Roll and Move; I have the second edition of this; Expansions: Zombies!!! 2: Zombie Corps(e), Zombies!!! 3: Mall Walkers, Zombies!!! 3.5, Zombies!!! 4: The End..., Zombies!!! 5: School's Out Forever, Zombies!!! 6: Six Feet Under, Zombies!!! 7: Send in the Clowns

RATING: 1
Ok, so 1 star is too harsh.  It's more like a 2, because the game is in fact playable, but I just want to emphasize you should not buy this game.  It came out in 2001 and that really shows.  The roll to move feature mean that about 1/3 of the time you will be moving either 1 or 2 spaces.  The game makes little to no sense how you are competing against each other to survive a zombie apocalypse.  And that only one person can make it to the chopper and survive, and that you can apparently fly a helicopter without issue.  Are we a group of trapped helicopter pilots?  Also, the combat is uninteresting.  Roll about a 3 to win, roll below to lose.  And worst of all, the game length is brutal, it's over an hour of this 1 game mechanic.

(Posted during the rate Zombies a 10 drive to support Todd's fight against Cancer. :( )

Zombies!!! is almost as popular as Munchkin and almost as bad of a game. The basic framework is functional enough. Place a tile, pick up some cards and waste some zombies. Unfortunately, it's all down hill from there. The combat system is so simplistic that it makes the game painfully repetitive and manages to feature almost every type of game mechanic that I hate. Gotcha! cards that prevent the leader from ever winning, Death penalties that are so severe it's like starting the whole game over and a win condition that is almost one hundred percent random. It's like this game was built specifically for me to hate.

Shoot this thing in the head and go buy Last Night on Earth already...

RATING: 3
Zombies!!! is a game that starts of with plenty of gusto and then slowly winds down as the board increases and as resources deplete. This is the real mood-killer of the game...you would think play would get more tense and exciting as more zombies emerge and as players are racing to collect trophies but such is not the case. By the final stretch of the game, the tedium and sluggish pace start to wear on the nerves. It's worth noting, however, that I've not played any later editions of Zombies!!! and thus can't speak to whether these issues have been addressed. House rules for more card-play and a few additional options could certainly help this game be a better experience.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
This was one of the few Zombie games available at the game store when I bought it.  It wasn't great then, and it definitely hasn't fared well through the recent board game renaissance this past decade.  

First, I really like tile laying games.  I really like Zombies.  I like chance games.  This seemed like it would be a good fit.  The problem with it is how it ends.  The person with the lowest zombie count gets to place the helipad when it appears.  This means that often they can place it right next to them and win while others are on the other side of the map.  Annoying.  

Several of the special cards only work if you are in a specific building which is really hard to ever get there so the card is useless.  Thematically great, but painful and pointless when playing.  Just throw those cards away because they aren't very likely to help you at all.  

There are times in the game when it makes more sense to die than live so you can start over from the fountain.  Silly thematically and annoying if someone uses this to win over what was your dominate position.  Lame.  

Players really are against each other rather than for each other, which again, seems rather silly for a Zombie outbreak where the few survivors would probably stick together, at least until they were a bit more in the clear.  

If you are looking for a Zombie game, go for Zombicide (tactical minis) or Dead of winter (strategic/betrayal/thematic).  Both are better games than this.  I only play this game when my nieces come over and they don't want to commit to longer game (like Zombicide) or they just feel like killing things with no consequence or thought.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
